<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en"><span dir="auto">Celine Dion singles discography</span></h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>

<p>The <a href="/wiki/Discography" title="Discography">singles discography</a> of Canadian recording artist <a href="/wiki/Celine_Dion" title="Celine Dion">Celine Dion</a> consists of 140 <a href="/wiki/Single_(music)" title="Single (music)">singles</a> and 5 <a href="/wiki/Charity_record" title="Charity record">charity records</a>. At age twelve, Dion collaborated with her mother and brother, Jacques to compose her first song, "<a href="/wiki/Ce_n%27%C3%A9tait_qu%27un_r%C3%AAve" title="Ce n'était qu'un rêve">Ce n'était qu'un rêve</a>", which was released as a single in <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a> in June 1981.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sylvain_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-sylvain-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> By 1983, she became the first Canadian artist to receive a <a href="/wiki/List_of_music_recording_certifications" title="List of music recording certifications">Gold</a> record in France for the single "<a href="/wiki/D%27amour_ou_d%27amiti%C3%A9" title="D'amour ou d'amitié">D'amour ou d'amitié</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> Further success in Europe came when she represented <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_1988" title="Eurovision Song Contest 1988">Eurovision Song Contest 1988</a> with the song "<a href="/wiki/Ne_partez_pas_sans_moi" title="Ne partez pas sans moi">Ne partez pas sans moi</a>", which later won the contest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1990, Dion made her debut into the American market with <i><a href="/wiki/Unison_(Celine_Dion_album)" title="Unison (Celine Dion album)">Unison</a></i>. The album included "<a href="/wiki/Where_Does_My_Heart_Beat_Now" title="Where Does My Heart Beat Now">Where Does My Heart Beat Now</a>", which became her first single to reach the top ten on the United States <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, peaking at number four. In 1991, Dion sang with <a href="/wiki/Peabo_Bryson" title="Peabo Bryson">Peabo Bryson</a> in the song "<a href="/wiki/Beauty_and_the_Beast_(Disney_song)" title="Beauty and the Beast (Disney song)">Beauty and the Beast</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> It became her second top ten <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 single, and won the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Song" title="Academy Award for Best Original Song">Academy Award for Best Original Song</a>, as well the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Pop_Performance_by_a_Duo_or_Group_with_Vocals" title="Grammy Award for Best Pop Performance by a Duo or Group with Vocals">Grammy Award for Best Pop Performance by a Duo or Group with Vocals</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> Her following single, "<a href="/wiki/If_You_Asked_Me_To#C.C3.A9line_Dion_version" title="If You Asked Me To">If You Asked Me To</a>", peaked at number four on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100.</p>
<p>Released in late 1993, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Colour_of_My_Love" title="The Colour of My Love">The Colour of My Love</a></i> spawned Dion's first US, Canadian, and Australian number-one single "<a href="/wiki/The_Power_of_Love_(Jennifer_Rush_song)#Celine_Dion_version" title="The Power of Love (Jennifer Rush song)">The Power of Love</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> In the United Kingdom, both the album and the single "<a href="/wiki/Think_Twice_(song)" title="Think Twice (song)">Think Twice</a>" simultaneously occupied the top of the British charts for five consecutive weeks. "Think Twice", which remained at number one for seven weeks, became the fourth single by a female artist to sell in excess of one million copies in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> Keeping to her French roots, Dion continued to release French language recordings between each English album. <i><a href="/wiki/D%27eux" title="D'eux">D'eux</a></i> was released in 1995 and amassed huge success with the single, "<a href="/wiki/Pour_que_tu_m%27aimes_encore" title="Pour que tu m'aimes encore">Pour que tu m'aimes encore</a>". The song reached number one in France, stayed at the top position for twelve weeks, and sold over 955,000 copies in France, alone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> "Pour que tu m'aimes encore" topped the charts in Francophone countries and also peaked inside top ten in the UK, Ireland, Netherlands and Sweden.</p>
<p>In 1995, Dion released "<a href="/wiki/To_Love_You_More" title="To Love You More">To Love You More</a>" in Japan, where it reached number one,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> selling over one million copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> As a result, she became the first non-Japanese artist in twelve years to garner a number-one hit on the <a href="/wiki/Oricon" title="Oricon">Oricon Singles Chart</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> Released in 1996, <i><a href="/wiki/Falling_into_You" title="Falling into You">Falling into You</a></i> featured the US chart topping single "<a href="/wiki/Because_You_Loved_Me" title="Because You Loved Me">Because You Loved Me</a>". Other successful singles from the album included "<a href="/wiki/It%27s_All_Coming_Back_to_Me_Now#C.C3.A9line_Dion_version" title="It's All Coming Back to Me Now">It's All Coming Back to Me Now</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/All_by_Myself#C.C3.A9line_Dion_version" title="All by Myself">All by Myself</a>", which bothed reached the top five on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> In late-1997 Dion released most-successful single of her career, the classically influenced ballad, "<a href="/wiki/My_Heart_Will_Go_On" title="My Heart Will Go On">My Heart Will Go On</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> Serving as the love theme to the 1997 blockbuster motion picture, <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">Titanic</a></i>, the single topped the charts across the world, and became Dion's <a href="/wiki/Signature_song" title="Signature song">signature song</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> "My Heart Will Go On" won the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Song" title="Academy Award for Best Original Song">Academy Award</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Original_Song" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Original Song">Golden Globe Award for Best Original Song</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> It gave Dion two additional <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Awards</a> for "<a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Female_Pop_Vocal_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Female Pop Vocal Performance">Best Female Pop Vocal Performance</a>", and the most coveted "<a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Record_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Record of the Year">Record of the Year</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> Both "My Heart Will Go On" and "Think Twice" have so over one million units in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> She's also one of the biggest selling female singles artists of all time in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In late-1998, "<a href="/wiki/I%27m_Your_Angel" title="I'm Your Angel">I'm Your Angel</a>", a duet with <a href="/wiki/R._Kelly" title="R. Kelly">R. Kelly</a> was released. It became Dion's fourth <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 number-one single and her second song, after "My Heart Will Go On" to debut at the chart's top position. Released in 1999, <i><a href="/wiki/All_the_Way..._A_Decade_of_Song" title="All the Way... A Decade of Song">All the Way... A Decade of Song</a></i> included the successful lead single "<a href="/wiki/That%27s_the_Way_It_Is_(Celine_Dion_song)" title="That's the Way It Is (Celine Dion song)">That's the Way It Is</a>", which reached number six on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100. After a two-year hiatus, Dion released the album, <i><a href="/wiki/A_New_Day_Has_Come" title="A New Day Has Come">A New Day Has Come</a></i> in March 2002. The first single from the album was the <a href="/wiki/A_New_Day_Has_Come_(song)" title="A New Day Has Come (song)">title track</a>, which peaked at number twenty-two on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, and spent twenty-one consecutive weeks at number one on the <i>Billboard</i> <a href="/wiki/Adult_Contemporary_(chart)" title="Adult Contemporary (chart)">Hot Adult Contemporary Tracks</a>, breaking the record for the longest span at the top.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> The previous record holder was Dion's own "Because You Loved Me", which lasted nineteen weeks at number one. Through 2006, Dion has logged 87 weeks atop the Hot Adult Contemporary Tracks chart, the most of any artist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2007, the single "<a href="/wiki/Taking_Chances_(song)" title="Taking Chances (song)">Taking Chances</a>" gave Dion ownership of the most top ten hits on the Hot Adult Contemporary Tracks, with twenty-one during the last two decades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p></p>
